</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 158px"><div style="width: 158px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 156px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Isbjerget.jpg" title="The Isbjerget housing project (Aarhus, Denmark), inspired by form and color of icebergs, 2013, by CEBRA, JDS Architects, Louis Paillard, and SeARCH"><img alt="The Isbjerget housing project (Aarhus, Denmark), inspired by form and color of icebergs, 2013, by CEBRA, JDS Architects, Louis Paillard, and SeARCH" data-file-height="4051" data-file-width="5267" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Isbjerget.jpg/234px-Isbjerget.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Isbjerget.jpg/351px-Isbjerget.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Isbjerget.jpg/468px-Isbjerget.jpg 2x" width="156"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Isbjerget" title="Isbjerget">Isbjerget</a> housing project (<a href="/wiki/Aarhus" title="Aarhus">Aarhus</a>, Denmark), inspired by form and color of icebergs, 2013, by <a href="/wiki/CEBRA" title="CEBRA">CEBRA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julien_De_Smedt" title="Julien De Smedt">JDS Architects</a>, Louis Paillard, and SeARCH
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
</ul>
<p>Since the 1980s, as the complexity of buildings began to increase (in terms of structural systems, services, energy and technologies), the field of architecture became multi-disciplinary with specializations for each project type, technological expertise or project delivery methods. Moreover, there has been an increased separation of the 'design' architect <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[Notes 1]</a></sup> from the 'project' architect who ensures that the project meets the required standards and deals with matters of liability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[Notes 2]</a></sup> The preparatory processes for the design of any large building have become increasingly complicated, and require preliminary studies of such matters as durability, sustainability, quality, money, and compliance with local laws. A large structure can no longer be the design of one person but must be the work of many.
<a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">Modernism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Postmodern_architecture" title="Postmodern architecture">Postmodernism</a> have been criticized by some members of the architectural profession who feel that successful architecture is not a personal, philosophical, or aesthetic pursuit by individualists; rather it has to consider everyday needs of people and use technology to create livable environments, with the design process being informed by studies of behavioral, environmental, and social sciences.
</p><p>Environmental <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a> has become a mainstream issue, with a profound effect on the architectural profession. Many developers, those who support the financing of buildings, have become educated to encourage the facilitation of environmentally sustainable design, rather than solutions based primarily on immediate cost. Major examples of this can be found in <a href="/wiki/Passive_solar_building_design" title="Passive solar building design">passive solar building design</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_roof" title="Green roof">greener roof designs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biodegradation" title="Biodegradation">biodegradable</a> materials, and more attention to a structure's energy usage. This major shift in architecture has also changed architecture schools to focus more on the environment. There has been an acceleration in the number of buildings that seek to meet <a href="/wiki/Green_building" title="Green building">green building</a> <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_design" title="Sustainable design">sustainable design</a> principles. Sustainable practices that were at the core of vernacular architecture increasingly provide inspiration for environmentally and socially sustainable contemporary techniques.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup> The U.S. Green Building Council's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a> (Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design) rating system has been instrumental in this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (July 2016)">quantify</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Concurrently, the recent movements of <a href="/wiki/New_Urbanism" title="New Urbanism">New Urbanism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metaphoric_architecture" title="Metaphoric architecture">Metaphoric architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Complementary_architecture" title="Complementary architecture">Complementary architecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Classical_architecture" title="New Classical architecture">New Classical architecture</a> promote a sustainable approach towards construction that appreciates and develops <a href="/wiki/Smart_growth" title="Smart growth">smart growth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vernacular_architecture" title="Vernacular architecture">architectural tradition</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classical_architecture" title="Classical architecture">classical design</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> This in contrast to <a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">modernist</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Style_(architecture)" title="International Style (architecture)">globally uniform</a> architecture, as well as leaning against solitary <a href="/wiki/Housing_estate" title="Housing estate">housing estates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">suburban sprawl</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup> Glass curtain walls, which were the hallmark of the ultra modern urban life in many countries surfaced even in developing countries like Nigeria where international styles had been represented since the mid 20th Century mostly because of the leanings of foreign-trained architects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_types_of_architecture">Other types of architecture</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stourhead_Pantheon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Stourhead_Pantheon.jpg/220px-Stourhead_Pantheon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Stourhead_Pantheon.jpg/330px-Stourhead_Pantheon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Stourhead_Pantheon.jpg/440px-Stourhead_Pantheon.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stourhead_Pantheon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stourhead" title="Stourhead">Stourhead</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wiltshire" title="Wiltshire">Wiltshire</a>, England, designed by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hoare" title="Henry Hoare">Henry Hoare</a> (1705–1785)</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landscape_architecture">Landscape architecture</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Landscape_architecture" title="Landscape architecture">Landscape architecture</a></div>
<p>Landscape architecture is the design of outdoor public areas, landmarks, and structures to achieve environmental, social-behavioral, or aesthetic outcomes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> It involves the systematic investigation of existing social, ecological, and soil conditions and processes in the landscape, and the design of interventions that will produce the desired outcome.  The scope of the profession includes <a href="/wiki/Landscape_design" title="Landscape design">landscape design</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Site_planning" title="Site planning">site planning</a>; <a href="/wiki/Stormwater#Stormwater_management" title="Stormwater">stormwater management</a>; <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">environmental</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecological_restoration" title="Ecological restoration">restoration</a>; <a href="/wiki/Park" title="Park">parks</a> and recreation planning; visual resource management; <a href="/wiki/Green_infrastructure" title="Green infrastructure">green infrastructure</a> planning and provision; and private <a href="/wiki/Estate_(land)" title="Estate (land)">estate</a> and <a href="/wiki/House" title="House">residence</a> landscape master planning and design; all at varying scales of design, planning and management. A practitioner in the profession of landscape architecture is called a <a href="/wiki/Landscape_architect" title="Landscape architect">landscape architect</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interior_architecture">Interior architecture</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Interior_architecture" title="Interior architecture">Interior architecture</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Rennie_Mackintosh_-_Music_Room_1901.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="440" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Charles_Rennie_Mackintosh_-_Music_Room_1901.jpg/220px-Charles_Rennie_Mackintosh_-_Music_Room_1901.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Charles_Rennie_Mackintosh_-_Music_Room_1901.jpg/330px-Charles_Rennie_Mackintosh_-_Music_Room_1901.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Charles_Rennie_Mackintosh_-_Music_Room_1901.jpg/440px-Charles_Rennie_Mackintosh_-_Music_Room_1901.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Rennie_Mackintosh_-_Music_Room_1901.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Charles Rennie Mackintosh – Music Room 1901</div></div></div>
<p>Interior architecture is the design of a space which has been created by structural boundaries and the human interaction within these boundaries.  It can also be the initial design and plan for use, then later redesigned to accommodate a changed purpose, or a significantly revised design for <a href="/wiki/Adaptive_reuse" title="Adaptive reuse">adaptive reuse</a> of the building shell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-intar.risd_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-intar.risd-39">[37]</a></sup> The latter is often part of <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_architecture" title="Sustainable architecture">sustainable architecture</a> practices, conserving resources through "recycling" a structure by adaptive redesign.  Generally referred to as the spatial art of environmental design, form and practice, interior architecture is the process through which the interiors of buildings are designed, concerned with all aspects of the human uses of structural spaces.  Put simply, interior architecture is the design of an interior in architectural terms.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Naval_architecture">Naval architecture</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Naval_architecture" title="Naval architecture">Naval architecture</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lines_plan_en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="744" data-file-width="1052" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Lines_plan_en.svg/200px-Lines_plan_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Lines_plan_en.svg/300px-Lines_plan_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Lines_plan_en.svg/400px-Lines_plan_en.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lines_plan_en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Body plan of a ship showing the hull form</div></div></div>
<p>Naval architecture, also known as naval engineering, is an <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a> discipline dealing with the <a href="/wiki/Engineering_design_process" title="Engineering design process">engineering design process</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">shipbuilding</a>, maintenance, and operation of <a href="/wiki/Watercraft" title="Watercraft">marine vessels</a> and structures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> Naval architecture involves basic and applied research, design, development, design evaluation and calculations during all stages of the life of a marine vehicle. Preliminary design of the vessel, its detailed design, <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">construction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_trial" title="Sea trial">trials</a>, operation and maintenance, launching and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dry-docking" title="Dry-docking">dry-docking</a> are the main activities involved. Ship design calculations are also required for ships being <a href="/wiki/Ship#Repair_and_conversion" title="Ship">modified</a> (by means of conversion, rebuilding, modernization, or repair). Naval architecture also involves the formulation of safety regulations and damage control rules and the approval and certification of ship designs to meet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Statutory" title="Statutory">statutory</a> and non-statutory requirements.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_design">Urban design</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Urban_design" title="Urban design">Urban design</a></div>
<p>Urban design is the process of designing and shaping the physical features of cities, towns, and villages. In contrast to architecture, which focuses on the design of individual buildings, urban design deals with the larger scale of groups of buildings, streets and public spaces, whole neighborhoods and districts, and entire cities, with the goal of making urban areas functional, attractive, and sustainable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-berkeley_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-berkeley-42">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>Urban design is an interdisciplinary field that utilizes elements of many built environment professions, including <a href="/wiki/Landscape_architecture" title="Landscape architecture">landscape architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">urban planning</a>, architecture, <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">civil engineering</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipal_engineering" title="Municipal engineering">municipal engineering</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> It is common for professionals in all these disciplines to practice urban design. In more recent times different sub-subfields of urban design have emerged such as strategic urban design, <a href="/wiki/Landscape_urbanism" title="Landscape urbanism">landscape urbanism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water-sensitive_urban_design" title="Water-sensitive urban design">water-sensitive urban design</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_urbanism" title="Sustainable urbanism">sustainable urbanism</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Metaphorical_.22architectures.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id='Metaphorical_"architectures"'>Metaphorical "architectures"</span></h3>
<p>"Architecture" is used as a metaphor for many modern techniques or fields for structuring abstractions.  These include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Computer_architecture" title="Computer architecture">Computer architecture</a>, a set of rules and methods that describe the functionality, organization, and implementation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computer_systems" title="Computer systems">computer systems</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Software_architecture" title="Software architecture">software architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hardware_architecture" title="Hardware architecture">hardware architecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Network_architecture" title="Network architecture">network architecture</a> covering more specific aspects.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Business_architecture" title="Business architecture">Business architecture</a>, defined as "a blueprint of the enterprise that provides a common understanding of the organization and is used to align strategic objectives and tactical demands",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OMG_BAWG,_Definition_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-OMG_BAWG,_Definition-44">[42]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_architecture" title="Enterprise architecture">Enterprise architecture</a> is another term.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cognitive_architecture" title="Cognitive architecture">Cognitive architecture</a> theories about the structure of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_mind" title="Human mind">human mind</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/System_architecture" title="System architecture">System architecture</a> a <a href="/wiki/Conceptual_model" title="Conceptual model">conceptual model</a> that defines the <a href="/wiki/Structure" title="Structure">structure</a>, <a href="/wiki/Behavior" title="Behavior">behavior</a>, and more <a href="/wiki/View_model" title="View model">views</a> of any type of <a href="/wiki/System" title="System">system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seismic_architecture">Seismic architecture</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Earthquake_engineering" title="Earthquake engineering">Earthquake engineering</a></div>
<p>The term '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seismic_architecture" title="Seismic architecture">seismic architecture</a>' or 'earthquake architecture' was first introduced in 1985 by Robert Reitherman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> The phrase "earthquake architecture" is used to describe a degree of architectural expression of earthquake resistance or implication of architectural configuration, form or style in earthquake resistance. It is also used to describe buildings in which seismic design considerations impacted its architecture. It may be considered a new aesthetic approach in designing structures in seismic prone areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup>  The wide breadth of expressive possibilities ranges from metaphorical uses of seismic issues, to the more straightforward exposure of seismic technology. While outcomes of an earthquake architecture can be very diverse in their physical manifestations, architectural expression of seismic principles can also take many forms and levels of sophistication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup>
</p>

</li>
<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A project architect is one who is responsible for ensuring the design is built correctly and who administers building contracts – in non-specialist architectural practices the project architect is also the design architect and the term refers to the differing roles the architect plays at differing stages of the process.</span>
</li>
